<rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Come on people! You have to know what to expect from these places when you go. Maybe my expectations are more fair growing up in the SGV.

It's 25 for a full body massage and $15 for a massage up stairs. I've been here a few times and what I can tell you is that they're fair and make a effort  to give you a pleasant experience.

When I went, I'm always greeted by the front manager. She asks if I want water or tea and if I want a man or woman.

**The thing about these Spas is that a lot of people come here for hard, deep tissue massage to get worked on. It's not like they don't know other things but I tell them to only use their hands. I don't like non of that elbow or forearm digging into my skin so give me some presure but don't kill a brother! I get what I want because I tell them in ENGLISH what I want. haha

Just thought I would point that out. It's honestly easier for them to give you a more relaxing massage so I know a lot of comments is how hard they massage you. You have to give them some good instructions. Everyone is different!</Review>

< review>
Little by Little is a true hidden gem at the Warm Springs district in Fremont, CA, close to where T4 is. They are tucked away in the corner of the shopping center and this place serves really delicious food! They currently only do to go orders only and all the staff members do their very best to maintain covid safety procedures. They do fusions of every cuisines and serve from pastas, sandwiches, rice plates, and sides. I really enjoyed their food so much that I 100% truly recommend the most! I got to try their vegetarian options which were the roasted garlic cauliflower truffle Mac and cheese, the rainbow salad, and mushroom coconut pesto curry.

I will review the roasted garlic cauliflower truffle Mac and cheese first! It was absolutely my favorite dish on the menu! The presentation of the Mac and cheese was beautiful with the breadcrumbs on top and the chives to give it a nice color. Literally I haven‚Äôt had Mac and cheese in so long and this brings back many memories but I liked this version MUCH BETTER! I love the addition of the truffle oil because I think it gave a nice fattiness to the dish but it wasn‚Äôt drenched in oil which that‚Äôs a good thing. The breadcrumbs gave the Mac and cheese great texture and I love the dish having some garlic as well. I actually do wish that the Mac and cheese was cheesier because Mac and cheese is supposed to be a cheesy dish and for me, I personally wanted more cheese not only to make a viral tik tok video but taste wise, I would have liked and tasted more cheese. I also didn‚Äôt see a lot of cauliflower unless it was cut up small which I appreciate so you don‚Äôt get huge chunks but I didn‚Äôt  taste cauliflower. Overall, my favorite dish on the menu hands down, I really recommend the Mac and cheese!

The rainbow salad is basically kale, baby spinach, red quinoa, cherry tomatoes, red cabbage, roasted white corn, crispy quinoa, with yuzu aioli, and gribiche sauce on the side. This was truly a rainbow salad! I saw a lot of color and the presentation of the salad was beautifully done! You get the freshness of the kale, spinach and love all the vegetables and fruits in the salad as well! The nuttiness of the quinoa was delicious which added a nice flavor aspect to the salad. On the dressing, I‚Äôm questioning why I got two dressings because normally  we would only see one dressing so the dressings don‚Äôt clash. I wish I only got one dressing instead of two different dressings but both of them tasted about the same in terms of flavor. If I were to choose, I feel like the yuzu aioli was better in terms of flavor and thickness. I thought the gribiche sauce was too thick for me but the yuzu aioli felt lighter; still a but thick but tasted better in my opinion.

The mushroom coconut pesto curry has button mushrooms, red quinoas, cauliflower, corn, and garlic rice. I loved the flavor of the coconut curry. I thought it was creamy, smooth, light, and it was mild. I also love the addition to the quinoa because that added flavor and texture. The mushrooms, I love too and that is like a substitute for meat so the seasoning was on point and definitely was fulling to eat. With the cauliflower, again I didn‚Äôt get a lot of cauliflower. I wish there was more and I wish the rice had more garlic because I didn‚Äôt get a lot of garlic. Overall, I‚Äôm super satisfied with this curry and loved all the elements of the curry!

Overall, Little by Little in Fremont is a true hidden gem in Fremont! I really recommend it and please support this business! They have put a lot of heart and soul to the food and the chef was great in putting everything together to make the dish perfect!< /review>

<text>What a hidden gem in Warm Springs. I have passed by this place for so many times without notice it.

We decided to give it a try on a beautiful weekend. Small restaurant but completely filled up on Saturday noon.

The food here is so delicious and the drinks are cute too.

Roast Bone Marrow: Personally I love the bone marrow a lot, and the sauce on the side is phenomenal.

Confit duck leg: Love the harmony of crispy duck skin and the tender duck meat!

Drinks:
Rose lemonade is delicious!

< name>
B. Li< /name>
< Date>
1559596976144<//Date>
<Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
It's about time Fremont gains a new restaurant with class.

The core cuisine is American & French tapas. The menu is subject to change and it's been suggested that foie gras might be served in the future.

The most notable items I had here was the bone marrow, short rib, and uni pasta.

The bone marrow is served with some bread and it's basically a pate. Very rich and flavorful, would be a great choice if you're looking for brunch.

The short rib's presentation is lovely, like a meadow encircled by a dark forest. The meat just falls apart with a slight push of the fork. The garnish adds a complexity to the meat's succulent texture and a small bite of the salad followed by the meat helps balance the flavors. It is by far my favorite dish as it is both a feast for the eyes and the mouth.

The uni pasta here is sure to convince anyone apprehensive of trying uni. The uni itself turns the dish practically into macaroni and cheese, but it doesn't have the smell or heaviness of cheese. The uni is light and custardy and goes great with the roe on top of the pasta. It almost tastes like a comfort food, but has the flavors of the sea incorporated into it. Definitely recommended.

Will come back soon to see how the menu evolves.< /Review>

<Name>Jonas Gebhardt</Name><time>1524431783413<//time><Rating>3<//Rating><Text>I came here for date night on a Friday evening without a reservation. I've learned that I should make a reservation next time in order to secure one of the few tables.

I ended up sitting by the bar which is not bad in any way as you get a good view on the kitchen and can see how everything is being prepared. I observed how the chef takes great pride in finishing off every dish before he sends it out and is focused on quality and a consistent experience.

Having that said, the dishes do look pretty and very presentable. I tried 4 dishes, plus desert and every dish was worth a photo. The first one I had was the Octopus dish. It's supposed to be a shareable dish, but the portion is still rather small and you only get a few bites of Octopus. All of that is fine in general, the issue is the prize. You pay over $20 for that dish and if you want to feed two people well, you need to order at least three more dishes - if not even four more. This means you will end up paying between $100-170 including drinks. I am ok to pay this kind of money for a nice dinner, but I expect the right service and taste then. Let me elaborate on this.

All dishes I had tasted solid, but there was nothing that really blew me away. Some dishes, like the Risotto are a great idea, but the flavor is not yet there where it needs to be. It felt too salty to me and too soft. I think it's a matter of time and the chef will turn this into a great dish.

Similar with the bone marrow. It's something that you don't eat every day and it was certainly well cooked. But it was missing that certain something that makes me want to end up spending so much money on it. For example, it comes with basic toast which feels just very boring.

The short ribs were solid as well, but not tender and juicy enough for the prize.

Again, there's nothing wrong with the food, but I think the chef just needs some time to refine and work on the recipes to justify the high charge.

The service was so-so. I've ordered a glass of the Cabernet from Passo Robles. One of my favorite wine regions and the red did not disappoint. But: they charge $12 a glass which is somewhat standard in the Bay area, but I never got poured less wine in a glass than here. It almost felt I get more wine when I go to a wine tasting. When I tried to bring this up with the waiter in a friendly and funny way and told him that I love this wine, he just mentioned he would let the chef know. I also asked if the Yelp check-in for 50% off cocktails would apply to wine, because I would take another glass if it would - he said no. I had two sips of the wine and the glass was empty. When I paid and was ready to leave, the waiter offered me another glass on the house - very wrong timing.

Overall the service was very friendly though and I ended up leaving a nice tip.

The place itself feels upscale, modern and cool. It could almost be in L.A. I feel it has huge potential but requires some serious work on the food, the prizes and the wine.< /Text><Pics>None</Pics><resp>None</resp><gmapID>0x808fc65b8df00001:0xc5005cf459a6b782</gmapID></record>

<text>I can see why temecula police have so many terrible reviews.  I was really disturbed to see a man in a busy Walmart parking lot holding a "please help" sign with a 4 year old. He went to his van at one point, without even telling his daughter, so she followed him.  Their van had the hood up like they were stranded too.  When he walked back to the corner to hold his sign up, he left and was not even paying attention to his 4 year old.  She would call out, "daddy" and try and get his attention.  He was ignoring her.
I called the Temecula police and the lady I spoke with sent a deputy out there.  She asked if I wanted a call back and I said yes.  About half hour later, I still see this man begging with his daughter again.  I got a call several hours later by a deputy who was clearly annoyed that I had called about this and kept saying, "mam, I saw the girl standing in the dirt area and she was not in the street"... I explained to him what I saw and how she was being ignored, wondering in the street where the cars were driving by.  He acted as if I was lying and was really rude.  I told him I was going to look into it further and he told me, "mam, I'm telling you the law, he was not committing a crime, he was on public property" we went back and forth and after the officer told me, "well, whatever, he was not breaking the law" Apparently child endangerment is not a big deal to the Temecula Police and it's just "whatever"...  I suppose if she got hit by a car or taken while he was clearly not watching her police might have cared.  So if you see someone begging for money on a corner with a young child who is clearly being ignored, do not waste time calling the police. <review>I was seen at Lodi Western Dental on Tuesday and Wednesday this week.  Having a phobia about going to the dentist, I put off making an appointment for several years.
Vanessa, the finance coordinator, was very nice, explained my options and answered all of my questions with a smile.  The oral surgeons and dental assistants were also very nice and gentle, which convinced me that my phobia & fears were unnecessary.
But the person that stands out most as making this an excellent experience for me two days in a row was the dental hygienist.  He was very professional, yet friendly and compassionate.  I needed an extensive deep cleaning & he did an excellent job.  First, he made sure I was relaxed and put my mind at ease by explaining everything ahead of time.  He adequately numbed my mouth so I didn't feel any discomfort, and he explained everything step by step so there were no surprises.  He reviewed the home care instructions with me several times both days, making sure I fully understood his instructions.  It is obvious that Hassan loves his chosen field of expertise.
I will not postpone having cleanings done in the future, as long as he is the hygienist!
Overall, from start to finish this was an excellent experience.  I will no longer postpone dental appointments based on my phobias.< /review><Pictures>None</Pictures>< response>
